Manuals

Azimut Owner’s Manual. All the manuals for all the equipment are in electronic form in my iCloud account.

See non-maintenance tasks

A guy on the Azimut Yacht Owners Club recommended his electrician who I thought could answer any questions I have about the electrical:

Here’s the number for the Azimut electrician I have used in the past… he’s great (covers NY and Florida!) his name is Matt +1 (954) 253-4591

Equipment

Engines

The engines are Volvo Penta D13 900. The make and model of the alternator on each engine is a Volvo 21429786, a 28v 110A alternator.

Volvo Electronic Parts Catalog

V-Ribbed Belt Part # 20430615

Serial numbers

Serial 20132108864
Serial 20132107808

Generator (Kohler 21EKOZD)

Operation Manual TP-7044

Thermostat, opening temp: 79ºC (175ºF)
High exhaust temperature shutdown: 60ºC (140ºF)
Pressure cap rating: 95 kPa (13.7 psi)

Oil

Volume: 11.2 liters
Recommendation: API: CI-4, CH-4, CG-4 class SAE: 10W-40/5W-40

Coolant

Volume: 4.4 liters
Recommendation: 50% ethylene glycol; 50% clean, softened water (HOAT?)

Maintenance & Service Parts

Part Description Part Number
Fuel Filter Element ED0021753200-S
Oil Filter ED0021752800-S
Seawater Pump Impeller Kit 229826
V-Belt (Seawater Pump) GM90645
Zinc Anode ED0090802840-S

Thrusters

Thruster make & model: Side-Power SEP 170/250 TC
Proportional Power controller: Side-Power PPC820

Batteries

The 12 house batteries are FIAMM VR850 (12v 95Ah). From what I can tell so far, they are wired in pairs in series and each pair is wired in parallel, therefore, effectively six 24v 95Ah batteries. Three appear to be for house/service batteries and the threeare for the starboard engine starter, although the Azimut wiring diagram shows them as a 4 and 2. Plus, there’s a separate starter battery that I haven’t figure out how is wired in yet.

The generator also has a battery for it. Haven’t yet opened the box to inspect it.

Spare Parts Inventory

The filters are for emergency use but also should be used when they need to be replaced because they have a shelf life. Plus, the D13 air filters are expensive ($200+/each!) so use them!

ⓘ
  1. Check the status of electrical connections in order to detect any presence of corrosion and / or oxidation (cable connection terminals, fuse holders, etc.).
  2. Check the correct tightening of the cable termination bolts.
  3. Check the conditions of cables, in particular whether there are any signs of exterior wear or damage to the cable isolation.
  4. Carefully check the status of any rubber gaskets or of the watertight doors of switch or control panels.
  5. Check conditions of grounding circuits
  6. Check the conditions of the grounding circuits, zincs and copper plates.

Electrical ▸ Open all battery boxes & inspect

{
  "uuid": "U9yUBrZwXXeGkUwZGbDDZx",

  "title": "Open all battery boxes & inspect",
  "notes": "Check the batteries, checking in particular for the presence of any oxidation on the terminals and acid on the battery body.\n\nMaintenance of terminals is essential because it is through them that the battery can supply power correctly to the systems. In particular, the positive terminal (+) of the battery, for chemical issues, is subject to sulphation becoming white with time (white lead sulphate crystals). This chemical compound tends over time to isolate the battery from the circuit, especially strongly lowering the maximum inrush current that the battery can supply.\nTo avoid this phenomenon, smear the terminals, possibly also the negative terminal, with common Vaseline grease: the terminals will be permanently protected with no other maintenance needed except for checking the grease status.",

ⓘ

Check the batteries, checking in particular for the presence of any oxidation on the terminals and acid on the battery body.

Maintenance of terminals is essential because it is through them that the battery can supply power correctly to the systems. In particular, the positive terminal (+) of the battery, for chemical issues, is subject to sulphation becoming white with time (white lead sulphate crystals). This chemical compound tends over time to isolate the battery from the circuit, especially strongly lowering the maximum inrush current that the battery can supply.
To avoid this phenomenon, smear the terminals, possibly also the negative terminal, with common Vaseline grease: the terminals will be permanently protected with no other maintenance needed except for checking the grease status.

Operation Manual TP-7044, p.75

  1. Stop the generator set.
  2. Remove the retaining cap and remove the reed valve for inspection. See Figure 3-12.
  3. Use a mild detergent to remove residue and oxidation from the reed valve.
  4. Clear blockage from the reed valve opening.
  5. Replace the siphon break if the reed valve is cracked or if the reed valve material has hardened or deteriorated.
  6. Install the reed valve into the mounting base with the valve downward. See Figure 3-12, item 2.
  7. Install and only finger tighten the retaining cap. Do not overtighten it. Note: Ensure that the siphon break’s cap is tight before operating the generator set.

ⓘ

Took it out, looks great at 290 hours. Ran it for 10 minutes or so and the impeller is not leaking.

Operation Manual TP-7044, p.74

  1. Press the generator set OFF/RESET button to shut down the generator set.
  2. Disconnect the power to the battery charger, if equipped.
  3. Disconnect the generator set engine starting battery, negative (- ) lead first.
  4. Close the seacock.
  5. Remove the seawater pump coverplate. See Figure 3-10.
  6. Remove the impeller.
  7. Inspect the impeller for damaged, cracked, broken, missing or flattened vanes. The impeller vanes should be straight and flexible. See Figure 3-11. Replace the impeller if it is damaged.
  8. Lubricate the impeller with soapy water before installation.
  9. Install the impeller. Note: During installation push and rotate the impeller in the same direction as the engine rotation until it is thoroughly seated in the impeller housing.
  10. Inspect the coverplate and gasket for corrosion and/or damage. Replace components as necessary.
  11. Lubricate the gasket with silicon grease and attach the gasket and coverplate to the seawater pump housing.
  12. Open the sea cock.
  13. Check that the generator set is OFF.
  14. Reconnect the generator set engine starting battery, negative (- ) lead last.
  15. Reconnect the power to the battery charger, if equipped.
  16. Start the generator set and check for leaks.
  17. Stop the generator set and repair leaks or replace damaged or worn components.

ⓘ

Operation Manual TP-7044, p.78

  1. Press the generator set OFF/RESET button to shut down the generator set.
  2. Disconnect the power to the battery charger, if equipped.
  3. Disconnect the generator set engine starting battery, negative (- ) lead first.
  4. Remove the belt guard. See Figure 3-17.
  5. Check the belt tension at the midpoint of the longest span of the belt by pressing with your finger approx. 10 kg (22 lbs.) of force. See Figure 3-19 for belt deflection ::10mm (0.4 inches)::. Recheck a new belt tension after 10 minutes of operation. If the belt tension is not within specification, go to step 3. If the belt tension is within specifications, go to step 7 10.
  6. Loosen the pivot and adjusting screws.
  7. While prying the seawater pump outward, tighten the adjusting screw.
  8. Tighten the pivot screw.
  9. Recheck and adjust as necessary.
  10. Replace the belt guard.
  11. Check that the generator set is OFF.
  12. Reconnect the generator set engine starting battery, negative (- ) lead last.
  13. Reconnect the power to the battery charger, if equipped.

ⓘ

Azimut’s recommendation (see below) for a disinfectant soluton using chlorinated bleach seems very high (128 fl oz per 100 gallons), which is 8 times higher than what The Water Quality & Health Council recommends, which is a much lower concentration (16 fl oz per 100 gallons) and that’s closer to other sources I’ve read about sanitizing RV fresh water tanks. Azimut’s procedure sounds good, at least. Perhaps this is a translation or metric-to-imperial conversion error on Azimut’s part?

The fresh water tank is 196 gallons (740 liters), so use 32 fl oz (1 liter) of bleach.

Azimut’s Recommendations

From page 203 of Azimut Owner’s Manual:

It is advisable to periodically treat the fresh water tank with a disinfectant solution to be poured into the tank through the refilling plug.

Once a year, when preparing for winter storage, treat the entire system with a concentrated disinfectant solution, opening all faucets in order to distribute the solution along the entire system, until emptying it completely.

  1. Wash thoroughly the entire system using potable water
  2. Empty completely the system
  3. Fill the entire system with a chlorine solution and let rest for at least one hour
  4. Empty completely the system
  5. Wash thoroughly the entire system using potable water
  6. Fill the system with potable water

4/24/2023

Check hydraulic steering oil level

ⓘ

From page 176 of Azimut Owner’s Manual:

Very little routine maintenance is required for the hydraulic steering system. What is essential is that the oil level in the system is checked. The tightness and lubrication of mechanical links between the rudder bar arms must be periodically checked. Check for excessive clearance between the shaft and supports.

In some rare occasions you may find air trapped into the pipes. It is generally caused by total or partial disassembly. In this case eliminate the air by opening the vent valve on the steering gear pumps of the wheelhouse (internal and flybridge) and turn the rudder to the left and to the right until the end stop to release the air in the pipes. While doing this, fill the hydraulic tank. All these operations can be carried out by your supplier at each seasonal check-up.

9/13/2023

Electrical inspections6 months

ⓘ
  1. Check the status of electrical connections in order to detect any presence of corrosion and / or oxidation (cable connection terminals, fuse holders, etc.).
  2. Check the correct tightening of the cable termination bolts.
  3. Check the conditions of cables, in particular whether there are any signs of exterior wear or damage to the cable isolation.
  4. Carefully check the status of any rubber gaskets or of the watertight doors of switch or control panels.
  5. Check conditions of grounding circuits
  6. Check the conditions of the grounding circuits, zincs and copper plates.

9/13/2023

Open all battery boxes & inspect6 months

ⓘ

Check the batteries, checking in particular for the presence of any oxidation on the terminals and acid on the battery body.

Maintenance of terminals is essential because it is through them that the battery can supply power correctly to the systems. In particular, the positive terminal (+) of the battery, for chemical issues, is subject to sulphation becoming white with time (white lead sulphate crystals). This chemical compound tends over time to isolate the battery from the circuit, especially strongly lowering the maximum inrush current that the battery can supply.
To avoid this phenomenon, smear the terminals, possibly also the negative terminal, with common Vaseline grease: the terminals will be permanently protected with no other maintenance needed except for checking the grease status.

Trapped air in the fuel system can cause difficult starting and erratic engine operation.\n\nPrime the fuel system under the following conditions: \n* Before starting the engine for the first time.\n* After running out of fuel and adding fuel to the tank.\n* After fuel system maintenance such as changing the fuel filter, draining the fuel/water separator, or replacing a fuel system component.\n\n**Note:** Connect the battery during the priming procedure to allow engine cranking.\n**Note:** Have a rag handy during this procedure. Check that the generator set is OFF.\n5. Reconnect the generator set engine starting battery, negative (- ) lead last.\n6. Reconnect the power to the battery charger, if equipped.\n\nSource: *Operation Manual TP-7044*, p.69-70\n",

3/16/2023

Replace fuel filter (every 250 hours or 3 months)

ⓘ
  1. Press the generator set OFF/RESET button to shut down the generator set.
  2. Disconnect the power to the battery charger, if equipped.
  3. Disconnect the generator set engine starting battery, negative (- ) lead first.
  4. Close the fuel supply valve.
  5. Loosen the fuel filter by turning it counterclockwise. Remove the fuel filter and use rags to clean up spilled fuel oil. Note: Dispose of all waste materials (engine oil, fuel, filter, etc.) in an environmentally safe manner and in accordance with all applicable laws.
  6. Clean the contact surface of the fuel oil filter adapter.
  7. Lightly lubricate the gasket surface of the new fuel filter with fresh fuel oil. Thread the filter on the adapter until the gasket makes contact; hand-tighten the filter an additional one-half turn. Wash hands after any contact with fuel oil.
  8. Open the fuel supply valve.
  9. Bleed the system. See Step 12 in the following procedure (secondary filter on 32- 40EKOZD/ 28-35EFKOZD models) or Section3.6.3, Fuel System Bleed (see below).

Source: Operation Manual TP-7044, p.68

Fuel System Bleed

Bleed air from the fuel system in order to reduce rough running or vapor lock. Trapped air in the fuel system can cause difficult starting and erratic engine operation.

Prime the fuel system under the following conditions:

  • Before starting the engine for the first time.
  • After running out of fuel and adding fuel to the tank.
  • After fuel system maintenance such as changing the fuel filter, draining the fuel/water separator, or replacing a fuel system component.

Note: Connect the battery during the priming procedure to allow engine cranking.
Note: Have a rag handy during this procedure. Wipe up any spilled diesel fuel. Wash hands after any contact with fuel.
Note: Dispose of all waste materials (engine oil, fuel, filter, etc.) in an environmentally safe manner and in accordance with all applicable laws.

Fuel System Bleed Procedure (14- 24EKOZD/12- 20.5EFKOZD Models)

  1. Loosen the fuel filter’s air vent screw. See Figure 3-5. Place a suitable container underneath to collect the fuel.
  2. Initiate the auto/start sequence until fuel, free of air bubbles, flows from the vent screw at the fuel filter.
  3. Tighten the fuel filter’s air vent screw.
  4. Check that the generator set is OFF.
  5. Reconnect the generator set engine starting battery, negative (- ) lead last.
  6. Reconnect the power to the battery charger, if equipped.

Source: Operation Manual TP-7044, p.69-70

3/16/2023

Check the heat exchanger anticorrosion zinc anode (every 250 hours or 3 months)

ⓘ
  1. Press the generator set OFF/RESET button to shut down the generator set.
  2. Disconnect the power to the battery charger, if equipped.
  3. Disconnect the generator set engine starting battery, negative (- ) lead first.
  4. With the generator set cooled, close the seacock, open the petcock on the engine, and drain the coolant into a suitable container.
  5. Remove the anticorrosion zinc anode (plug) from the heat exchanger.
  6. Use a wire brush to remove the loose corrosion on the anticorrosion zinc anode. Replace the anode according to Figure 3-15 and Figure 3-16. ::Dimensions of new anode: 14.5mm diameter, 40mm length. Replace when length or diameter is < 50%::
  7. Clean the threaded hole of the heat exchanger and coat the threads of the anticorrosion zinc anode (plug) with pipe sealant suitable for marine applications. Cut the anticorrosion zinc to the correct length. Install the anticorrosion zinc anode into the heat exchanger.
  8. Close the petcock on the engine and open the seacock. Refill the cooling system.
  9. Check that the generator set is OFF.
  10. Reconnect the generator set engine starting battery, negative (- ) lead last.
  11. Reconnect the power to the battery charger, if equipped.
  12. Start the generator set and check for leaks at the anticorrosion zinc anode location. The pump is operating if the cooling water flows from the exhaust outlet. If water is not discharging at the exhaust outlet, see Section 2.1, Prestart Checklist--Seawater Pump Priming.

9/7/2023

Generator: Replace the oil in the crankcase & replace filter (every 500 hours or 6 months)6 months

ⓘ

Oil Specifications

Viscosity: SAE 10W-40/5W-40
With Specifications: API CF, CI-4, CH-4, CG-4

Drain the oil (Whenever possible, drain the oil while it is still warm)

  1. Press the generator set OFF/RESET button to shut down the generator set.
  2. Disconnect the power to the battery charger, if equipped.
  3. Disconnect the generator set engine starting battery, negative (- ) lead first.
  4. Remove the oil drain hose from its retaining clip. Remove the cap from the oil drain hose and lower the hose into an oil collection container. Electric Oil Drain/Oil Fill Pump Procedure: Connect the pump to the end of the oil drain hose. Place the outlet of the pump into an oil collection container. Remove the oil fill cap(s).
  5. Open the oil drain valve on the engine.
  6. Allow time for the engine oil to drain completely. Electric Oil Drain/Oil Fill Pump Procedure: Activate the pump until all of the oil is removed. Go to step 2. Note: Dispose of all waste materials (engine oil, fuel, filter, etc.) in an environmentally safe manner and in accordance with all applicable laws.
  7. Close the oil drain valve.
  8. Replace the cap on the oil drain hose. Replace the oil drain hose in its retaining clip.

Replace oil filter

  1. Remove the oil filter by rotating it counterclockwise with an oil filter wrench.
  2. Apply a light coat of clean oil to the rubber seal of the new oil filter.
  3. Install the new oil filter following the instructions provided with the filter.

Fill with oil

  1. Add new oil of the weight, grade, and quantity specified in Section 3.5 (see above too). Electric Oil Drain/Oil Fill Pump Procedure: Disconnect the pump. Close the oil drain valve. Replace the cap on the oil drain hose.
  2. Check for leaks
  3. Check that the generator set is OFF.
  4. Reconnect the generator set engine starting battery, negative (- ) lead last.
  5. Reconnect the power to the battery charger, if equipped.
  6. Start the generator set and check for leaks around the oil filter.
  7. Stop the generator set and tighten the oil filter to stop any leaks.

Note: Dispose of all waste materials (engine oil, fuel, filter, etc.) in an environmentally safe manner and in accordance with all applicable laws.

Source: Operation TP-7044 manual, p. 67

9/3/2023

Disinfect fresh water tank6 months

ⓘ

Azimut’s recommendation (see below) for a disinfectant soluton using chlorinated bleach seems very high (128 fl oz per 100 gallons), which is 8 times higher than what The Water Quality & Health Council recommends, which is a much lower concentration (16 fl oz per 100 gallons) and that’s closer to other sources I’ve read about sanitizing RV fresh water tanks. Azimut’s procedure sounds good, at least. Perhaps this is a translation or metric- to-imperial conversion error on Azimut’s part?

The fresh water tank is 196 gallons (740 liters), so use 32 fl oz (1 liter) of bleach.

Azimut’s Recommendations

From page 203 of Azimut Owner’s Manual:

It is advisable to periodically treat the fresh water tank with a disinfectant solution to be poured into the tank through the refilling plug.

Once a year, when preparing for winter storage, treat the entire system with a concentrated disinfectant solution, opening all faucets in order to distribute the solution along the entire system, until emptying it completely.

3/20/2023

Wash gel coat

ⓘ

Wash the gelcoat surfaces with non-abrasive equipment (non-scratch sponges, cotton or micro-fiber fabrics, medium/soft brushes) and a low alkaline detergent (to avoid degrading the layer of protective wax) that does not contain silicone or oils. During the summer months, it is advisable to wash down twice a month if the boat is used frequently. During the winter, maintenance may be reduced if the boat is hauled and covered.

3/20/2023

Clean windshield wipers and nozzles

ⓘ

From page 183 of Azimut Owner’s Manual:

The operational area of ​​the windscreen wiper must be free of obstacles. Frequently check the correct operation of the windscreen wiper. Make sure the nozzles are operating correctly. If, when under way in rough sea, the salt spray accumulates on the windscreen, operate frequently the windscreen wipers to prevent salt water crystals from damaging the windscreen or the wiper arms.

Prolonged exposure to the sun and to the marine atmosphere causes premature wear of the windscreen wiper rubber arms.

Once a month (or when required) thoroughly clean the windscreen wiper with a neutral detergent or with a specific solution for the glass, while the arms should be cleaned with a damp cloth. When cleaning, check the edges of the arms. If the rubber is deformed, damaged, or cut, or if the windscreen is not clean enough, replace the wipers to prevent damaging the windscreen.

Once every two months (or when required) clean the nozzles by inserting a needle into the holes in order to free them from any salt crystals and lime deposits.

3/20/2023

Clean Teak Decks

ⓘ

Kill Mold

If there’s mold, use vinegar and water solution (1:16) first to kill the mold.

Clean

  1. Rinse with water
  2. Squeegee standing water off
  3. Pour undiluted Simple Green on and scrub with a somewhat stiff brush in a circular motion
  4. Rinse and squeegee off standing water
  5. Wipe down with a cloth

Restore golden color

  1. Use Teak Cleaner part 1
  2. Rinse
  3. Use Teak Cleaner part 2
  4. Rinse

Azimut’s recommendations

From page 186 of Azimut Owner’s Manual:

Teak has natural properties that make it ideal for the marine environment. When your boat is new, teak has a light golden color; you would like to maintain this color. Unfortunately, teak is very sensitive to light and fades after a prolonged exposure to sunlight. The best way to preserve the deck teak original color is to clean it periodically with a soft brush and with plenty of FRESH water. In this way it is possible to clean the pores of the wood and destroy algae that form when the fresh water stagnates for a long period. It has been found that when stubborn dirt or consistent stains cannot be removed, a hard sponge with a small amount of NEUTRAL SOAP can be used.

Do not be afraid to use large quantities of water on the teak since water helps maintaining the balance of the wood, especially in very hot weather.

If you prefer the color of weathered teak, remember that the natural process will stabilize it after a few months giving the wood a light gray color.

The best way to keep the teak in these conditions is to clean it periodically with a soft brush and with plenty of SALT water.

We do not recommend the use of protective oils because they penetrate deeply and, under the influence of heat and humidity, can have negative effects on teak joints. Varnishes and lacquers can eventually ruin teak.
The use of a powerful cleaner is not recommended as high pressure water jets may cause ruptures between the sealing material and the sides of the joint.

Varnishes and lacquers can eventually ruin teak.\nThe use of a powerful cleaner is not recommended as high pressure water jets may cause ruptures between the sealing material and the sides of the joint.",
